    \n There are also more "unofficial" LE playbooks out there. Like Johnstone's Horsemen of the Apocalypse set, which includes badass ones like The Infernal and The Sorcerer. I have a photocopy of somebody else's photocopy that I treasure dearly. The playbooks aren't quite as "balanced" (whatever that means) as the official ones, but the moves are simply delicious. "When you bite someone with your giant toothy maw..." Oh yes. I almost took that one in the last AW game I played in.

    \n Challenge Accepted! Here I am, faceless: http://yfrog.com/h8xxcyj

    I also have a question for everyone. Someone outside my gaming group has asked me if I can pass on the Quarantine playbook PDF to them. Is it okay to do that? They've offered to swap for the Hoarder, but I already have that one. I'm less inclined to trade readily available playbooks, but you can't really get the Quarantine any more. Does that make it okay? Or worse? :S I don't want to violate any copyright or anything by spreading work, like these playbooks, that isn't mine to spread.

    What's the etiquette here?

    \n
    \n Oh snap, Bret has thrown down the gauntlet!

    Since he was kind enough to provide the playbook to me prior to the throwing of this gauntlet up in, I will endeavor to produce a photo of me in a hockey mask or something equally hokey.

    I have the Maestro D' and the Quarantine, and I'll share them freely in exchange for participating in this thread (even if you have already!): Apocalypse World: Custom Moves Make the Game! One valid participating act (name a move, craft mechanics for another) per playbook! Just whisper me when you do it, I don't need proof or anything.

    I have the other playbooks, but there are official ways to get your hands on them and I'd not step on anyone's creative toes by subverting that.

      Posted By: J. WaltonThere are also more "unofficial" LE playbooks out there. Like Johnstone's Horsemen of the Apocalypse set, which includes badass ones like The Infernal and The Sorcerer. I have a photocopy of somebody else's photocopy that I treasure dearly.
      \nThis is hilarious! It makes me feel like the old days, when I used to make demo tapes. Except I don't think anybody ever wanted one of my tapes enough to copy a copy.

      I still have a few of these booklets left that are available for trade, actually.

      \n
      \n\nChroma \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Posted By: BenhimselfHas Vincent ever stated a policy on how he feels about public trading or giving-away-for-challenges the limited playbooks? Besides by their creators?
      \nFrom an email that directed me here from Vincent himself:

      > The Maestro D' was available as a limited edition for people who
      > preordered, the Faceless is a limited edition I bring to cons with me,
      > and the Quarantine is a limited edition for people who supported
      > Joshua AC Newman's Shock:Human Contact kickstart. They aren't
      > officially publicly available now; I may rerelease them in some form
      > later on, but I don't have any definite plans.
      >
      > However, I'm pretty sure that if you ask around - at Story Games, for
      > instance - you'll find somebody who'll set you up.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nmease19 \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Posted By: BenhimselfHas Vincent ever stated a policy on how he feels about public trading or giving-away-for-challenges the limited playbooks? Besides by their creators?
      \nI wish I could find the post but I think he basically felt like creators should have the right to distribute their creations and for his stuff, he liked the idea of exclusives being exclusive and said that, ideally, everyone would have a different mix of materials. That said, I'm pretty sure he's ok with people distributing materials to players in their games (e.g. if you were MCing a game you could give a playbook to a player that wanted to play it). That's my interpretation of his intent anyway.
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nJ_Walton \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n My sense is that the limited playbooks are supposed to be cool collectibles and acquiring them is supposed to involve actual social interactions with other excited AW fans. So, just posting them openly for download is not cool (impersonal, effortless). But interacting with people and acquiring the playbooks that way is cool.
      \n

      \n\nJoshua A.C. Newman \n\n\n

      \n
      \n
      \n

      Of all the playbooks, the Quarantine \u2014 part of a promotion for Shock:Human Contact \u2014 is the one that should be most contagious. That means to me that, if you want a copy of Quarantine, you have to play Human Contact with someone who's got it \u2014\xa0that is, someone who backed the project on Kickstarter, or someone who played with someone who backed the project. Those people are the ones who were promised a special bennie for backing the game, so it's up to them if they want to infect you with it.

      \n

      But I hear the newer strains are even more problematic: it might be a rumor, but someone told me the Quarantine can be passed on by simply tweeting, blogging, or posting about Human Contact play!

      \n

      Or biting.

      \n

      (Consentual only, please!)

      \n\nJoli \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n ROLE PLAYING CHALLENGE for the Maestro D':

      First, the Maestro D's flavor text:

      In the golden age of legend, there was this guy named Maestro. He was
      known for dressing up real dap and whever he went, the people had much
      luxe tune. There was this other guy named Maitre d\u2019. He was known for
      dressing up real dap and whever he went, the people had all the food they
      could eat and the fanciest of it.

      Here in Apocalypse World, those two guys are dead. They died and the fat
      sizzled off them, they died same as much-luxe-tune and all-you-can-eat. The
      maestro d\u2019 now, he can\u2019t give you what those guys used to could, but fuck it,
      maybe he can find you a little somethin somethin to take off the edge.

      Play or MC a session of Apocalypse World. Invent and use a Custom Move for a character who could be a Maestro D'. post the move and describe how it worked out, just a few sentences is fine, in this thread. And whisper your email to receive a Maestro D' playbook!

      NON-ROLE PLAYING CHALLENGES for the Maestro D':

      -Cook me a meal and serve it to me. Doesn't have to be a three-course dinner, but it at least has to be lunch. "Serve" can be interpreted forgivingly.
      -Sing me a song of your own devising, with an apocalyptic theme.
      -Play me a song of your own devising on the musical instrument of your choice.

      The first one of course is limited in time and space, but I'm sure you savvy computerheads can find a way to bridge that spatial gap.

      And whisper your email, etc!

      Peace,
      -Joel
      \n

      \n\nNick Doyle \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n edited March 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n One morning not too long ago, the Maestro and his people showed up at the gate. Not the docks like sane people, mind you. The gate. Meaning they'd come through the Maze, and Marsh's savages. We let them in since they didn't look like trouble and it was clear they had some jingle. Figured they'd stick for a couple days and then head down-harbour like most folks. Turns out this Maestro D feller (and we're still not sure if that's his name or his title; guess it don't matter much), he rented one of Fat Mike's empty buildings and moved in. You can see it from Market, it's the one with the awning that's been painted up all bright colours. Nobody knew what to make of these folk until they put the hand-painted sign up. Three words for everybody to see, and they don't leave any doubt about what they've got on offer in there. The sign says it all.
      \n
      \nWhen you have sex with any of the Maestro's well-oiled manwhores at the EatDrinkFuck, roll+hard.
      \n On a 10+ there's no problem, you don't come down with that new rash that's going around.
      \n On a 7-9 it'll be a day or so before your skin starts to get discoloured and flakey, y'know, down there. A quick trip to Boo's clinic will cost you 1-barter and some scolding, but you'll be fine.
      \n On a miss, you wake up the next morning itchy and flaking everywhere. Hopefully Boo is secretly fond of you, because you're about to become a full time job for her. If she can't (or won't) help you, you'll quickly learn why all of the Maestro's people are scantily-clad and oiled, as the feel of cloth on your skin becomes unbearable and only the Maestro's oils and ointments offer relief. Fortunately, he's always looking for new talent...
      \n
      \nOf the PCs, only the hardholder Marco has availed himself of the Maestro's services, and he's been fine. But since the chopper Daff left town on an errand to a distant hold, his special lady friend Joe's Girl has been screwing Maestro every chance she gets. The infection is coming on hard, but she's been able to hide from folks for now. She's not going to the clinic because everybody knows Boo's assistant Mox can't keep his mouth shut and she's worried what Daff will do if he gets back and finds out. The Maestro's been making friends with all the right people in town, but Joe's Girl is well liked, especially by the chopper gang and Want's cultists. If things go badly for her (and they look like they will), the resulting tussle could tear the whole town apart...

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nzipht \n\n\n

      \n Vic, wasn't sure when the Maestro setup his den. Lot's of people where selling sex on the Wreak. It wasn't till those mushrooms showed up that he took interest. Where did these mushrooms come from? How did Maestro come to have so many..

      When you take, your gang to the Maestro's to take off the edge. Roll+Barter Spent. On a hit, you and your gang had a fucking great time. The MC might ask you a question or two; answer them. On a +10 drop a Want from your gang, they are loving life. This want wouldn\u2019t fuck you till they suffer a lost, again. On a 7-9 You guys can\u2019t stop talking about going back. Gain a +1 Ongoing when motivating your gang with promises of returning. Loose, +1 Ongoing when you, spend jiggle on some other bullshit. On a Miss your gang and you are now addicted to the Maestro\u2019s drugs gain Want: Drugs.

      The game I am MCing takes place on a Beached Aircraft Carrier, called The Wreak. This move is motivated for us to learn more about the Hard-holder. I'd love feedback on this move. I plan on using it tomorrow night.
      \n

      \n\nNeurook \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n When not busy serving as personal chef to the king of Container City, Maestro D sits in his steel hut sharing his gift with those who bring him fresh or not quite so fresh ingredients.
      \nThe results are often delicious, sometimes dangerous and always weird.
      \n
      \nWhen you make Maestro D cook something for you roll +Barter spent.
      \n
      \n10+: The meal turns out incredible and literally blows your mind.You automatically open your mind to the maelstrom and succeed like you had rolled a 10+
      \n7-9: The meal was unique, but has left you feeling all weird inside. You gain a +1 forward when next opening your mind to the maelstrom, but take -1 ongoing until you do so.
      \nMiss: The meal turns out disgusting, but Maestro D makes it clear that "he cooks it, you eat it". You automatically open your mind to the maelstrom and fail.
      \n
      \nI'm thinking being fed by this guy day in and day out has made the king turn just a little loopy, I guess we'll see tomorrow.
      \n

      \n I've already got the Maestro'D playbook, but I can't resist. Not very refined yet, but I have to get back to work...

      He Knows What You Did Last Summer: when you first meet the Maestro'D, choose another PC, and roll+ their Hx with you. On a 10+, the Maestro doesn't know a thing about you that your buddy doesn't already. On a 7-9, choose 1:

      - You've kept a secret from the PC. What is it, and how did the Maestro find out?
      - You took something from the PC. What is it, and how did the Maestro get her hands on it?
      - You took someone from the PC. Who is it, and how did the Maestro get her hands on him?

      On a miss, respond with fuckery, including anything from the list that fits the bill.

      \n\nJoli \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Great Moves, everyone!

      Nick, love the rash. that's awesome. I like how it's not just, "you get a rash and it sucks!" but rather, drags you into this whole web of obligations.

      Zipht, pretty cool. I like the 10 is a benefit, the 7-9 a benefit with a dependency, and the miss just dependency. There's a nice symmetry there.

      Ross, that song is pitch-perfect. Everybody click through and listen to Ross' song!

      Neurook, love the brain-opening. Normal activities that open your brain are rad. -1 until you open is particularly slick.

      Joe, great use of Roll +Hx! And nice list of consequences.

      I need a description of play from most of you. When you use it in a game, or if you have already, post a sentence or two here (more if you want) and BAM, playbook!

      Sorry for the delay, folks. I'll email playbooks as soon as I'm home from work!

      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n Since the Sight For Sore Eyes bundle is over, as co-creator of the Hoarder, I will make you a special deal.

      Do something genuinely nice and helpful for another person. (Nice AND helpful. Not tough love, not "you look nice today." Do something good and be good about the way it's done.)

      Donating money for things like Japan is awesome, and you should do it anyway, but not for this. This is about seeing the good you do make a direct impact on someone else. It's important.*

      You can tell me what you did, or just tell me you did it. It's the honor system, because if you have a soul, making up something really nice you pretended to do for someone just to get something free on the Internet should make you feel like a dirtbag.

      Hooray!

      *And also addictive. I try to do this every day. I don't always succeed, but man, it's like crack.

      \n I finally sent out playbooks! Sorry to keep people waiting. Anyone else want to take the Maestro D' ROLEPLAYING CHALLENGE?

      I've had a taker on the NON-ROLEPLAYING CHALLENGE as well, to my surprise! If anyone else wants to cook me food, I live in Portland, OR. You may a;so find me at Fabricated Realities in Olympia in June, or Go Play NW in Seattle in July!

      Peace,

      \n Simon,\n
      Posted By: ElizabethSince the Sight For Sore Eyes bundle is over, as co-creator of the Hoarder, I will make you a special deal.

      Do something genuinely nice and helpful for another person. (Nice AND helpful. Not tough love, not "you look nice today." Do something good and be good about the way it's done.)

      Donating money for things like Japan is awesome, and you should do it anyway, but not for this. This is about seeing the good you do make a direct impact on someone else. It's important.*

      You can tell me what you did, or just tell me you did it. It's the honor system, because if you have a soul, making up something really nice you pretended to do for someone just to get something free on the Internet should make you feel like a dirtbag.

      Hooray!

      *And also addictive. I try to do this every day. I don't always succeed, but man, it's like crack.
      \nThis post might interest you!

      \n\nJ_Walton \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n edited April 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Hey, I have a deal for anyone with the Maestro D (I have a print copy, but not PDF), the Faceless, or the revised Touchstone (whenever it becomes available). I'll trade you a "supplemental playbook" containing 3-5 custom moves and/or gear, written specifically for the playbook of your choice (preferably for a character type you're already playing in an ongoing AW game), all laid-out in a nice spiffy PDF.

      Your supplemental playbook can represent a specialization, a "prestige class," a body of lore or skills, some special equipment, or whatever other theme you like. You pick the foundational playbook and the theme, I write the moves and do layout on the PDF. Obviously, your MC doesn't have to let you buy these supplemental moves with advances, but I'll take the care to make them really solid and badass, so your MC will look like a jerk for disallowing them

      Then, if you like, you can trade that mini-playbook for other things, expanding the barter economy. Only you and I will have copies, initially, and we'll see how they spread.

      P.S. If you're interested, whisper me what playbook you want to trade, what playbook you want moves for, and your preferences as far as theme goes. If I get a bunch of offers, I'll pick the ones that most inspire me.
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n First book in the Saga of Pliocene Exile
      \n
      \nStarts in the Future; The Latent metapsychic powers of humans have become fully operant. Human embrace Unity with Alien races ....
      \nBut, some misfits, rebels & adventurers decide to leave through a one-way time portal to simpler, less perfect times; Earth's Pliocene epoch.
      \nThere they find a race of Latent metapsychic aliens; the Tanu(Fey like) & the Firvulag(Giant, Goblin & Orc like).
      \nThe Tanu have made themselve almost full psychic operants through the use of Torcs; gold, silver and grey(to control / enslave)
      \nThe Firvulag are naturally operant to a lesser degree, mostly in creating horrific illusions.

      \n\namnesiack \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Posted By: Brendan ConwayChris, I'm totally fine with that trade.

      If anyone else wants the Wurm, all you have to do is recommend a cool book to read, and explain why you're recommending it. Any kind of book is great, although I am envisioning non-fiction books.

      \nI love recommending books!

      Nonfiction, eh? Hmm...

      The last really good nonfiction book I read was Girls to the Front: The True Story of the Riot Grrrl Revolution. Riot Grrrl was really influential on me in my early teens, but in a many-steps-removed sort of way, since I was living in a small Arkansas town. It's really interesting to me to see how the whole thing started, what it became, and how the version of it at that reached those of us far away was filtered and changed in translation. It's probably not going to be super interesting to everyone, but if you have interest in DIY organization/culture, music (particularly punk music), or a youth take on modern feminism, it's pretty rad.



      \n

      \n\nrian_bean \n\n\n

      Posted By: Brendan ConwayChris, I'm totally fine with that trade.

      If anyone else wants the Wurm, all you have to do is recommend a cool book to read, and explain why you're recommending it. Any kind of book is great, although I am envisioning non-fiction books.

      \nFiction: Maul by Tricia Sullivan
      Futuristic feminist sci fi novel. Young girls hang out at the maul and wreck havoc.. "a maelstrom of violence and shopping". Men have been almost wiped out by something called the "Y-Plagues". I haven't finished it yet, but its great so far- super, super smart writing, and not what I expected in re: plot line when I picked it up. The book jacket says is "Sherri Tepper meets Neal Stephenson" and thats pretty spot on.

      Non Fiction: "Mountains beyond Mountains" and "Strength in What Remains", both by Tracy Kidder, both about the people and the work being done by Partners In Health, a non profit group of doctors and advocates (and more specifically, Dr. Paul Farmer) in Haiti and other countries. Infuriating and inspiring, all in one. You learn way more about the depressing and screwed state of the world health crisis than you probably wanted, but then you get to learn about great people trying to change things. If I had a hero, it would be Paul Farmer.

      Yay! I like these challenges.

      \n
      \n\nEsoteric \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Book recommendations:
      \nI'm not a big nonfiction reader, but I can see a few good ones on my shelf, so here goes.
      \n
      \nThe Master Magicians: Their Lives and Most Famous Tricks
      \nExactly what it says on the tin. This collection of short biographies tells the story of "the golden era of modern magic", focusing on the creation of the magician's signature tricks, and the experiences surrounding them. The writing can seem dry and impersonal, but occasionally the author slips up and reveals his true passion for the subject. This book shows a major hallmark of a good biography, in that reading it makes me enthusiastic about a subject I otherwise wouldn't even think about.
      \n
      \nThe Encyclopedia of Bad Taste
      \nStarting with Accordion Music and working it's way down to Zoot Suits, this book archives anything and everything worthy of disapproval. A good deal of it is made up of smarmy commentary on dated fads (see: fuzzy dice, lawn ornaments), but it also has some truly fascinating articles, such as "Death Cars of Famous People" and a particularly long entry on the Lawrence Welk Show. Did you know that because of Welk's fixation with bubbles, the technicians for the show had to devise an entire network of fans, allowing the bubbles to drift about the stage, while preventing them from getting soap grease on the floor or instruments? Now you do.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nBenhimself \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Nonfiction Book: Fair Division, by Steven Brams and Alan Taylor. Starting with classic "cake-cutting" problems for two or more people ("I cut, you choose") and moving onto more complex forms of envy-free dispute resolution, an excellent reference to have in mind when exploring a world defined by scarcity of important resources.

      And now, working on a Hocus Supplement called The Witch-King that's just a couple of moves that give you creepy and obviously unnatural powers to call upon. A teaser: the move you get automatically once you decide you're playing a Witch-King:

      Bargaining: Tell the MC the price you have paid for your power. If they are impressed, choose an extra Witch-King move. If they're not impressed, they'll provide you with three prices they /would/ find impressive: you can choose one, in addition to the price you willingly paid, to choose an extra Witch-King move.



      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nApril 2011 \n edited April 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Brendan: Site Analysis and Landscape Graphics.
      \n
      \nThey're basic texts on mapping and analysis for landscape architecture, architecture, and urban design, both pretty slim and introductory. Site Analysis is the more general of the two books, since it talks more broadly about collecting and diagramming information. Landscape Graphics is much more focused on diagrammatic maps ... not useful to everyone, but we're all gamers here, so I reckon we all have at least some interest in making sharp-looking, information-rich maps.
      \n
      \nThey're very good: lightweight, with clear language and lots of graphic examples.

      \n\nJohnstone \n\n\n

      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n A book recommendation for Brendan Conway:

      Bury Me Standing: The Gypsies and Their Journey by Isabel Fonseca.

      This is a good book to read if you are interested in different types of history, and insurmountable walls between different cultures.

      The gypsies wander throughout Europe, completely devoid of prosthetic information technology: they have no archives, no chronicles, no historical records; not even an oral history the way First Nations have history. They have stories about times long ago, but they don't care about origin stories, even their own. Few gypsies are interested in their journey out of India and all across Europe, as chronicled through music by Tony Gatlif in the film Latcho Drom.

      Any lessons they learn throughout life are passed on to future generations as habits and behaviours or fictional stories, not as records. Their nomadic habits and disdain for records and private property put them directly at odds with modern states and modern society (a situation that reminds me of the explanation of Anglo-Irish difficulties given by Henry Hobhouse as part of his history of potatoes in Seeds of Change). The difficulties that the few Western-educated gypsies have in crossing between, and even attempting to unite, these two worlds speaks volumes about the gap that exists.

      \n\nJoli \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n edited April 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n For Brendan:

      Inventing the Child, by Joseph L. Zornado

      This book is a mind-blowing and scathing look into the true purpose of children's literature (and adult literature for that matter)--to reproduce the dominant ideology in succeeding generations and thus "invent" the child in the image of the adult. Zornado's shocking but coherent claim is that, for hundreds if not thousands of years, adult culture has been squelching children's basic emotional needs. Childrearing practices are aimed at breaking the will of the child and subjugating them to the adult, and condemning any show of honest emotion as "rebellions" and "willful". The child thus broken grows up and perpetuates the cycle by buying into the philosophy and transmitting it to their own children. And the literature of the day reflect that, and propagate it.

      Highlights:\n
        \n
      • Freud's Seduction Theory, which suggested the emergence of repressed trauma memories were the result of adult abuse, and which he abandoned in the face its implications for his culture and his family, and put forward the Oedipal Theory, which suggests that the child's inappropriate desires are at fault.
        • \n
      • Lewis Carroll's Alice in Wonderland, how it relates to victorian predatory objectification of the ideal child, and how a writer steeped in the dominant ideology can propagate it even as he seeks to critique it.
        • \n
      • A scathing expose of Walt Disney's empire, the abusive parental relationship it emulated behind the scenes, the themes of adult-child subjugation in major films from Pinocchio to the Lion King, and the appropriation of the very concept of childhood for consumerist purposes.
        • \n
      • The raw honesty of Maurice Sendak's children's books, and the boiling childhood rage latent in the stories (i just started this chapter myself).
        • \n
      As a new parent, it's pretty brutal reading. It's not the smoothest read--Zornado never uses a simple and direct word where an erudite circumlocution would be suffice--but I'm finding it worth the effort. It's also related (indirectly, because I hadn't yet read Inventing the Child when I wrote it) to the emotional core of my game, The Dreaming Crucible, for whatever that's worth.

      Peace,
      -Joel

      Posted By: J. WaltonI'll send this one to anyone who posts an anecdote from their play experiences about something or someone from an AW character's past coming back to haunt them.
      \nSo, when I made Angler, my Maestro D for a PbP over at RPG.net, I went with the "tattooed face" because, tattoos, tres hot, am I right? And I thought about it, and decided he probably had full-body tattoos, he just covered most of it up with his immaculate whites (including gloves). And then I thought a bit about where he got them. In the end, I decided that he had been born into a water cult (the game was set in a desert town, so it seemed apropos) that kind of imploded on itself by his early teens, getting freaky and degenerate towards the end of things. He moved on to a place far away, and made a new life for himself.

      Now, I kept this past a secret (including, foolishly, from the MC, because at the time I was excited about the idea of it being revealed in play through the psychic maelstrom's questions, and also we had a brainer and a savvyhead as PCs so if I hooked them up with anything odds are good details would come out), but that backstory really ended up influencing the character. There were a lot of small details, like the fact that he purified his own water despite being rich enough to buy it at the town's market, or the way he used water-based metaphors to refer to the world's psychic maelstrom all the time like "taking a dip", but the big thing was that he was really wary of cults in general. Or rather, he was suspicious of the motives of people in charge but sympathetic to the "ordinary" people who were just caught up in the tide of things, so to speak. And how people reacted to the town's own cult (unrelated to his own) strongly influenced his opinions of them: if they thought the cult was a potential problem to be watched, he respected them a bit more, if they slept around with the cult's leader, he... didn't, quite so much.

      So in the end, I'm satisfied with how the character's past backstory influenced his present, and he was definitely more than a little bit haunted by it even though he hid it well, but in hindsight, my anecdote's going to be a cautionary one: share that shit, explicitly, with the MC. Because when I think about it, if the game had continued instead of falling to the curse of most PbP games, having a NPC wander into town with the exact same tattoos as Angler, with all the speculation that would have raised and dancing around Angler would have had to do to keep all his private demons from coming out of the woodwork that that would have entailed, would have been totally awesome. Here's hoping the Loner makes that sort of dream a reality!
      \n

      Posted By: J. WaltonI'll send this one to anyone who posts an anecdote from their play experiences about something or someone from an AW character's past coming back to haunt them.
      \nThis was from an online game so I have written out answers to the MC's character questions:
      "How I got here...
      Sewie showed up around the 'scrapers a couple years back. Nothing special, he just floated in one day. When anyone asks, he happily relates how he was rescued from the sinking remains of his former ship by a couple heading South in the Dirty Blond. They were very nice to him and he speaks wistfully about the woman's beauty and the man's good nature. Unfortunately, the man was washed overboard in a particularly heavy storm. Sewie never did mention what became of the woman."

      We also wrote about our Hx with the other PCs.
      "Sewie is pretty comfortable around most folk, he don't ask for much in exchange for his services, but he'll let you know if he thinks you're trying to take advantage of him. Unless you're 'Rielle that is. ...but she usually shows up with Boo, so he just keeps his mouth shut, head down, and acts like she's not there. Who knows what's going on there... What would people think if she told them that she knows what happened to that woman on the boat? [Tell everyone else Hx+1. Everybody knows a bit about who you are and where you\u2019ve been.] "

      I think you can see where this is going... I never did decide what happened to the woman, I just put it in another player's hands and trusted her to make it interesting!

      \n @ Brendan
      \n
      \nFor your book club.
      \n
      \nThe Ghosts of Cannae: Hannibal and the Darkest Hour of the Roman Republic
      \nBy Robert L .O'Connell
      \n
      \nMore than just a book about the 2nd Punic War, it discusses the Battle of Cannae and how it almost destroyed the Roman Republic. Highlights include:
      \na) Hannibal's defeat of a numerically superior army by exploiting the weaknesses of Rome's military structure and tactics.
      \nb) The slaughter of a significant portion of Rome's political/military elite, and its effect on Roman politics over the next few decades.
      \nc) How this battle helped force the Roman military to evolve further from it's Greek roots, and, as a result, became the military machine behind the Roman Republic/Empire
      \n
      \nWas trying to think of something more apocalyptic, but this is a pretty great book.

      Posted By: J. WaltonI'll send this one to anyone who posts an anecdote from their play experiences about something or someone from an AW character's past coming back to haunt them.
      \nI had an operator named Nero who worked inside the hardhold New Jerk, ruled by the ruthless Daimyo. I didn't always agree with what he did, and on one occasion I disobeyed a direct order, but mostly we worked together. However, he started getting out of hand with the conquest, mustering up as big an army he could and taking on another hardhold in direct assault, and Nero sorta got dragged in. The battle didn't go very well and the moment he realised the other hold had a mortar (or some such) he blew off the attack and his player retired him to safety. Nero, having lost almost his entire crew in the battle, and the third character, Canaveral the Battlebabe turned Angel, took this opportunity to bail New Jerk, moving north to get away from it.

      Three sessions later, after skipping about a year of in-game time, something in Nero's pack starts crackling and buzzing. It's the old walkie-talkie he used to talk to Daimyo! Daimyo, now an NPC, has heard of the adventures of Nero and Canaveral and needs the latter back at the holding to take care of a disease. Canny immediately decides she should go there to help, but Nero requires quite a bit of persuasion before going back to New Jerk, and the moment he's escorted Canny there, he rides off to never be seen again (retire to safety). Just being around New Jerk, risking getting involved in Daimyo's schemes again, was too much.


      Book recommendation for the Wurm:

      Non-fiction (?): The Physics of Superheroes. Explains basic concepts of physics with examples based on superheroes, and details what they get wrong and the few times they actually get something tricky exactly right. This was the book that opend my eyes to the concept of the "miracle exception" in fiction - you have a premise which blatantly breaks some law of physics or fundamental of our world, but given that premise everything else is realistic or at least believable. They also deduce the size of krypton based on the tatement that the early superman could jump over a ten-storey building.

      Fiction: World War Z: an oral history of the zombie war. The best example I've seen of the above-mentioned miracle exception. The traits of the solanum virus are detailed, unrealistic as they may be, but the rest of the book just follows, y'know? Everything from how to most effectively kill zombies, how the first outbreaks happened, how countries reacted and what the world looks like when it's over - nothing feels made up or unrealistic one you accept how the virus works. The style of the book (transcriptions of interviews with survivors) helps with this, and all in all it's a great read.

      I can be reached at jonatan.kilhamn-at-gmail.com
      \n

      \n\nJohnstone \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Two bonus recommendations for Brendan (and anybody else who wants to impress anthropologists, historians, or smarty-pants):

      On Deep History and the Brain, by Daniel Lord Smail.

      Smail argues that history pays too much attention to written documents, and replicates Biblical origin narratives by starting history in Sumeria. He argues for more integration of pre-history and "primitive" man, and wants to see more history that takes evolution into account. He also writes about the neurochemistry of the brain and how psychotropic drugs (including caffeine) physically change the brain, and how that may have affected human culture in history. Not so much a catalogue of answers as intriguing questions.

      The Power of Babel: A Natural History of Language, by John McWhorter.

      If you only ever read one book about language and linguistics, read this one. McWhorter provides clear explanations of the various aspects of language, including grammar, structure, words, language change, pidgins and creoles, dictionaries, the politics of languages and dialects and what the difference is, why people think the Inuit have a billion words for snow, what fucking insertion is, and a whole bunch else. This book will tell you how humans actually use language, not how people think you should be using it.
      \n

      \n\nAysez \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Posted By: Brendan ConwayChris, I'm totally fine with that trade.
      \n
      \nIf anyone else wants the Wurm, all you have to do is recommend a cool book to read, and explain why you're recommending it. Any kind of book is great, although I am envisioning non-fiction books.
      \n
      \nHere's a book that I love to death:
      \nGnosticism: New Light on the Ancient Tradition of Inner Knowing by Stephen Hoeller.
      \nIt's a great starting point for anybody interested in learning about Gnosticism. Aside from being a big go-to in quite a few gaming books, it's interesting in and of itself. Seeing how things could have turned out differently if only for a few things is great, and it is a fascinating read.
      \n
      \nAs a bonus, here's another one:
      \nConsciousness and Mental Life by Dr. Daniel Robinson
      \nThis one illustrates Psychology's roots from ancient philosophy to its modern incarnation. I had the great fortune to have the author as a professor, and the syllabus for the semester was essentially this book. It covers a lot of territory, and I highly, HIGHLY recommend it to anybody with even a passing interest in philosophy of mind. I will warn you, though, it's a bit dry in parts.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nTristansaurus-Rex \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I think I would have to recommend to Brendan a pair of books.
      \n
      \nNon-Fiction: The Art of Falconry, by Emperor Frederick II known as Barbarossa. Best translation is done by the Standford University Press. It is considered to the text on falconry. It's an interesting read, and a skill that could come in handy after the Apocalypse.
      \n
      \nFiction:In keeping with the Apocalypse World, I would have to offer up Cormac McCarthy's novel, The Road. It got made into a movie recently. But as with just about every other book, it is better than the movie.It is about a father and son traveling through the wasteland of the world after a cataclysm which killed the majority of the world's population.
      \n
      \nTo whomever it was that was talking about writing Playbooks, I thought it would be cool if someone came up with something like a falconer and call it something cool like The Raptor. I would, but I am fairly new to the system.

      Posted By: Tristansaurus-RexTo whomever it was that was talking about writing Playbooks, I thought it would be cool if someone came up with something like a falconer and call it something cool like The Raptor. I would, but I am fairly new to the system.
      \nI think you can model this pretty easily with an Operator with an animal crew (Gigs: Surveillance for scouting, Deliveries for messages, Scavenging for hunting game, etc).

      That said, it's definitely a concept that could be reinforced by a few custom moves. Hmmm.

      \n
      \n BTW, the Catalyst is also done now and is my new favorite, alongside the Loner. There's something really amazing and powerful about writing moves that are just about a perspective rather than a separate set of powers or abilities. That's something I really have to remember.

      I'm super proud of Lead by example, which is a Battlebabe-style leadership move where people tell you stuff, back up your play, and fight alongside you without you having to do anything, just because you're a total badass. It's also the only move I know of that starts, "When you mark XP, hold 1."

      You can get a copy of the Catalyst by doing something AW-related for someone else. You can give them one of my playbook supplements for free, write them a custom move, run a session for other folks, draw them a picture or a map, or something else. Whisper me your email and I'll send it along.

      \n
      \nThe Valkyrie and The Fallen have been finalized. Johnstone and George Cotronis have copies, respectively, so talk to them or me. Here's a sample move from each one:

      Wake the dead: When you celebrate and mourne those who\u2019ve recently fallen in battle, you pull their souls\u2014or something resembling them\u2014through the Psychic Maelstrom to this world. Roll+barter spent. On a 10+, all of those fallen make the crossing relatively safely and join your ghost army. On a 7-9, one or more souls arrive, but tattered and torn by the Maelstrom. On a failure, a few souls come across, but they do not join your army, having more pressing business.

      Space oddity: You\u2019ve brought something back with you, in your mind, and it wants to get out. Whenever you open your brain, a nearby person takes \u03a8-harm. If you\u2019re touching someone, it\u2019s them.
      \n

      \n Okay. I think I'll post one anyway, maybe it will inspire somebody else:

      A new move for Brainers:

      Extra-Sensory Perception: When you extend your senses past their physical limits, roll+weird. On a 10+, choose 2. On a 7-9, choose 1:
      * You may ask a question from the read a sitch list about a remotely-viewed scene.
      * You may view a scene for an extended period of time.
      * You may view a scene that is very far away.
      * You may view a scene with all five senses.
      On a miss, you experience prophetic visions, are overwhelmed by the psychic maelstrom, or form a persistent connection with a person, place, or thing related to your viewing.

      \n\nfealoro \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n edited April 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n George Cotronis, what do you think about this Savyhead move?
      \n
      \nGIVE MY CREATION LIFFEEE!: When you try to implant some tech directly to a person Roll+weird. If you have a life support add 1. On 10+ choose 2 boons and 1 drawback. With 7-9 choose 1 boon and 1 drawback.
      \nIf you miss the MC choose 1 drawback or simply the gear doesn\u2019t work.
      \n
      \nBoons
      \nThe gear you have implanted work properly when in use
      \nThe implant heal the patient to 6:00
      \nThe gear gives +1 each time the patient do the \u201copen your brain\u201d move
      \nThe implant cancel a debility
      \nThe patient and his gear are ready before a couple of weeks.
      \n
      \nDrawbacks
      \nthe patient gain a debility
      \nyour life support blows up. If you don\u2019t have a life support, your workspace falls apart
      \nthe gear, when not in use, sometimes can act on its own
      \nthe gear has a weird connection with the maelstrom and can attract it
      \nOn each miss using the gear the MC can use \u201cin brain puppet string\u201d to the patient as he has 1 hold instead of one of his moves
      \n
      \nYou can use the move more than one time on the same patient and gear as long as you can get some interesting drawbacks
      \n
      \n
      \nps apologize for poor wording
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n George, I'm not great at running mechanics but I thought of an interesting idea for the Touchstone that I kinda pulled from Book of Eli.
      \n
      \n(Used in conjunction with Know your Enemy)
      \nLast Bastion of Hope: When attempting to defuse a situation roll+hard.
      \nOn 10+ target backs down and buries the hatchet.
      \nOn 7-9 Good news! You've taken the attention off of the target, bad news is that the target wants you now.
      \nOn a miss, you've made it worse. The situation explodes.
      \n
      \nHope that this is decent enough to warrant The Fallen

      \n\nSteerpike \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Last week I got to change my Battlebabe Kite over to the Catalyst, and thus use the Lead by example move. Which thus far is my favorite move yet, matter of fact every single Catalyst move is like a love letter of awesome to the type of things I want to do when I play the Battlebabe. Anyway, back to what happened....

      Prior to this Kite was a directionless killer in the employ/servitude of the hardholder Parson, but over the events of the last few sessions and a little nudge from both Lemma the Savyhead and a slaver named Judge pushed Kite to pickup her shotgun and make the world into something she wanted. Lucky for me I had both Sharp and Hard highlighted so the killing of Judge and his goons to free a town gave me the advance I needed to grab Lead by example (Which gives you hold by earning EXP that you use to set things in motion around you and have people fight with you).

      As we left the town, the characters over in another part of the map unleashed a flood of nightmares from the psychic maelstrom that was going to crush the town we just liberated and allied with\u2026 so naturally Kite needed to go back and protect what she started and leapt into the defense of the town earning EXP and some hold\u2026 which I immediately spent to have the free slaves, surviving ex-slavers and townsfolk form a small gang around me and fight for the town which lead to more EXP and a larger gang and then victory. By this time I had another advance and a nearby gang so Kite picked up Leadership and a gang to take back to the hardhold for some bigger changes.

      See, while we were gone the Touchstone Hurricane kinda sparked a huge revolt in Parson\u2019s Hardhold, which lead to Kite\u2019s lover Cryn taking over. So when Parson returned he immediately moved to put the rebellion down\u2026 during the subsequent fighting I spent hold to learn what had happened, have soldiers on both sides back my play to end the fighting and thus ended up sitting on the throne sharing the rule of the hardhold with Parson. For now.

      - Colin

      \n\nApril 2011 \n

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nColin: Awesome. Lead by example might be my all-time favorite move right now. It's certainly my favorite of those I've written. I'll be interested to hear how Lead by example and Leadership work together, because I was figuring they'd be two different takes on the same thing and it'd be unlikely for one character to have multiple leadership moves (Pack alpha, Leadership, Frenzy, Lead by example, Hivemind, etc.).

      Matt: I wanted a less crazy font that could be paired with VKS VERY MUCH or whatever the main AW font is called, especially on the covers where I wanted the text to be readable when really small (like the "a Hoarder supplement for" text). Minion SmallCaps seemed like a good choice, which then led to its use on the interior as well. So, yeah, a conscious decision but not too well thought-out. I tend to pick fonts more by instinct than anything else.

      \n Starting work on a playbook expansion for the Quarantine called 'The Major' for Quarantines who want to build manpower and resources to continue their original mission. Here's the prototype move that started this line of thinking:

      One for the team: at the beginning of a session, you may change one of your highlights to Harm. Whenever you roll+harm taken, mark experience.

      Thinking of a good move sort of in between fortunes and pack alpha for recruitment. You'd get a stat called manpower that you roll at the beginning of each session to rebuild your gang and armory. Also thinking of moves that will make use of the stasis chamber the Quarantine has access to.
      \n
      \n

      \n
      Posted By: George CotronisI'll trade The Fallen for any AW-relevant AP (bite size or otherwise) or a new Move for anexistingPlaybook.
      \nHere's a move for the Angel playbook:

      Angel of Vengeance: When you declare vengeance against someone who has hurt you or someone under your protection, roll +harm taken. On a 10+, hold 3. On a 7-9, hold 1. If the harm that triggered your declaration resulted in death, any hit counts as a 10+.

      Spend hold on a one-to-one basis. All effects last until your vengeance is complete or until you make a move unrelated to your vengeance.
      * You know exactly where they are.
      * Take +1 forward on direct, violent actions against your target and all they hold dear.
      * The next time they see you, the glory of your countenance overwhelms them. They hesitate until you break eye contact, as per the Battlebabe move (whose name I cannot remember.)
      * When you open your mind to the psychic maelstrom concerning your target, any hit counts as a 10+.
      * Mark an XP every time you cause your target horrible, irrevocable loss.

      On a miss, they know that you are coming and they are not afraid. Take -1 forward until your vengeance is complete.
      \n

      \n Posted By: George CotronisI think that's the whole point, isn't it. Trading?
      \n
      \nTrading is one thing, I'm also talking about straight-up giving people stuff. That's the part I was getting caught up on. I don't want to undermine other people's trade set-up, but there is a point where people have everything and it leaves newer seekers out in the cold. That's my take on it anyway.

      \n\nSteerpike \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2011 \n edited May 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Posted By: J. WaltonColin:Awesome.Lead by examplemight be my all-time favorite move right now. It's certainly my favorite of those I've written. I'll be interested to hear howLead by exampleandLeadershipwork together, because I was figuring they'd be two different takes on the same thing and it'd be unlikely for one character to have multiple leadership moves (Pack alpha, Leadership, Frenzy, Lead by example, Hivemind, etc.).
      \nUntil I read this it didn't occur to me that they were the same type of move but in hindsight they totally are.

      Grabbing Leadership just seemed to fit the fiction at that point and I imagined that it was for the core group of followers and that further use of Lead by example would result in replacement gang members or more people joining in.

      Sadly the game seems to be done now, so I won't get a chance to play Kite anytime in the near future or use Social Engineering.

      - Colin
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nsimonwolf \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMay 2011 \n edited May 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Trading is one thing, I'm also talking about straight-up giving people stuff. That's the part I was getting caught up on. I don't want to undermine other people's trade set-up, but there is a point where people have everything and it leaves newer seekers out in the cold. That's my take on it anyway.
      \nI don't see anything wrong with it, for what it's worth. I share the playbooks I receive with my friends because, well, I think they're cool, and I want to share them with like-minded people who aren't the kind to post on forums like these. I don't expect anything in return except some good discussion and talks about the material, which seems like enough to me - as neat as the trading system people are setting up can be at times, it does often feel like people are being exclusive for the sake of being exclusive.

      Do what you want, I don't think anyone is really going to mind if you don't expect anything in return for getting people excited/interested about the game.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

    • \n

      \n I would rather you use mine (the Witch-King) as an incentive to encourage somebody to make something new, even if it's just a little thing like a single custom move for an existing class or such, than just give it away. But if you give it away so they can have leverage to get other cool stuff in trade, and propagate my work further, I wouldn't really feel [i]bad[/i] about it or anything.
      \n

      \n Posted By: FigureFourPosted By: BenhimselfI would rather you use mine (the Witch-King) as an incentive to encourage somebody to make something new, even if it's just a little thing like a single custom move for an existing class or such, than just give it away. But if you give it away so they can have leverage to get other cool stuff in trade, and propagate my work further, I wouldn't really feel [i]bad[/i] about it or anything.
      \nThis goes for mine (the Devoted) as well. Seems like a good principal in general.
      \n
      \nFair enough to both of you. I just figured after the 5th or 6th request for stuff I should at least, you know, ask people.

      \n\nChristopher \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2011 \n edited June 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      One problem with putting in the LE playbooks is that most of them are lone characters. With only the base playbooks, there's a better chance you'll end up with a Hardholder, Hocus, or Chopper who come with groups of people and start out tied into some fiction.
      \n
      \n
      \nEh. That's never really a concern of mine. A game with pure "loner" characters is fine.
      \n
      \nAlso, the Hoarder is the only real loner in the game and only strictly in the mechanical sense. All the others almost always end up as a part of a group, per the improvements.
      \n
      \nIn fact, the only playbooks I would think twice about dropping on the table would be the Hoarder and the Driver. Both change the game.
      \n
      \nThe Hoarder, in my experience, can sometimes leads to strong player conflict, which I love, but I know others don't. The other players sometimes don't see why the Hoarder can't just give them things to solve all their problems, when it's usually really clear to the Hoarder why this is a bad idea real quick.
      \n
      \nThe Driver makes the game world larger by existing. As the book says, a Driver needs places to go and reason to go there. A small hold standing against the wastes is a different game with another known, reachable hold. Not better or worse, just a different game.
      \n

      \n\nChristopher \n\n\n

      \n
      Posted By: FigureFourSince you're up for doing more tricks, I'll offer you the Devoted (an add on for Brainers who form a "romantic" relationship with the Psychic Maelstrom) to you and anyone else who will tell me about your character's relationship with the psychic maelstrom or about how the psychic maelstrom had agency in your game.

      If you haven't had a psychic maelstrom with agency, or haven't played yet or something like that, I would also accept your coolest idea about what the maelstrom could be.

      \nSweet. The Red was a red dust cloud entity that tore things apart, both literally and figuratively, and examined them. Sometimes it would rip an entire house apart, holding every single independent thing inside suspended, seeing how it worked, how it fit together. It sometimes came down like a fog, trying to force its way into people's heads, either to work its alien will through them or to force them to do something and then examine the social results. It once stole a girl, Shamrock, and a few months later, ejected her as a gift for the Hocus. Except now, she was absolutely catatonic and covered with lines and lines of senseless dogma, tattooed head to toe.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nmiedvied \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Since I haven't played yet, I will offer my coolest idea(s):

      1) You know those old stories (hailing to Asimov, I think, by way of Ellison) of robots interpreting their directive to do no harm - by action or inaction - to their human progenitors as requiring their active intervention to keep humans from harming themselves? That happened. Sadly, entropy is what it is, and the system meant to keep the humans entertained (essentially a networked VR simulation) broke. The humans remain locked in, glitching into and out of deeper levels of network access ("open your brain"). The simulation is running down, though, with energy supplies and raw materials running low, and the machine is prioritizing de-commissioning human minds by those who express an implicit death wish by failing to survive in simulation. The maelstrom is the busted network; death is being unplugged to die, mewling and screaming inside an iron sarcophagus; the best you can hope for is to be the last survivor, the last to die in your metallic crib. I like bleak.

      2) Sooner or later humans were going to develop inductive current tech that would allow them effective telepathy. They built it. They scattered it around the earth. Satellites in the sky; seeds in the ground; the entire world moved on from VoIP to VoB(rain)P. That's it. That's all the maelstrom is. There was no great and sudden end; nukes didn't crash into cities like falling angels; nor did God smite the unworthy from the face of his earth. The apocalypse didn't come because people were just too sinful, or were ridden with hubris, or reached too far or accomplished too little. The apocalypse wasn't a bang: it was a whimper. It was the open-eyed consumption of limited resources, it was laughing in the face of the poor while they died of curable illness, it was the rising price of education in a knowledge-based world. It was the occasional dip of history into dark ages, with recovery barred in one simple way: easily mined metals were already mined, easily burned fuels were already burned, nothing had been left to rebuild with. We don't live in the shadows of past greatness: we live in the shadows of past stupidity, living not with the memory of a lost golden age, but with a scowl cast on old fool's gold.

      3) The end was an alien invasion. Well, not invasion, so much as colonization: they didn't come with anything malicious in mind, anymore than the bacteria colonizing your skin come with harm in mind - either when they're there as pleasant old commensals, or when they break free into opportunistic infection. Some people didn't take too well. Actually, a lot of people didn't take too well, mostly those with certain protein aggregates in the brain. We lost all the old folks, and a lot of the middle-aged. With them, the knowledge base of our society was decapitated. The 'alien' in question is adapted to interstellar travel, and as such communicates not by sound waves but by EM pulse. Here, it's colonized human brains - and the local brain EM interference occasionally results in snatches of underlying thought patterns entering the consciousness of the creature. It's motives - it has some sentience when in high density clusters - now consist of keeping the humans alive, generally. It's not all-good, though: better to kill off a diseased calf than let it infect the herd, after all. It's not a guiding angel so much as an inhuman shepherd.

      Yeah, I guess the general pattern is that I don't get off on actual 'psychic' stuff. If I were to do something like that, I guess I'd go with the Maelstrom being the hopes of generations yet unborn, trying to birth themselves through guiding their f'n idiot ancestors. Or maybe go ghost-story, and make it the aggregate "unfinished business" of the various ghosts. It'd be fairly unhelpful in that scenario, unless a PC's goals lined up with those of a particular spook, and have definite swathes of bugfuck crazy and blind-eyed fury mixed in there. I guess it'd basically be an entire world living in The Sixth Sense.
      \n

      \n\nsohum \n\n\n

      \n\nJune 2011 \n edited June 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Oh, and an interesting idea I've had for the psychic maelstrom, as a sort of more grounded justification for the basic way people tend to make it behave...

      ---

      The end wasn't bad. It was \u2014 you know the old canard of techno-utopic Singularity? The Transcendence victory in so many civ-building games, the glorious dream of Stross, and Kurzweill, and Egan? It was that. It was meant to be beautiful, and perfect, and to take us beyond our petty, petty lives...

      Except it wasn't purely good, either. Like everything, we fucked it up.

      So what we have left are the descendants of the poor motherfuckers who were unwilling. Or unworthy \u2014 no global agenda, just poor planning and localised dickishness. Ten percent of the world's population were left behind, in all, the rest dropping where they fell, bodies rotting from accelerated decomposition agents.

      Now these people were dumped in a world where every bit of matter is computronium. This is why they go crazy, you know: your brain configuring and reconfiguring and error-correcting because it swears it sent that signal and it's expecting that foot to step up only it doesn't because some transcendent human-like being's sweeping through and chewing up and spitting out your electrons for it's own goddamn purposes. Only those really good at blocking it out, most of the time, survive.

      ---

      So, in play, opening your mind to the maelstrom is essentially becoming a more receptive bit of computronium. And so a lot of the ascendent beings compute their fuckin' compute functions in your head for a spell, and your brain makes the best sense of it that it can. They're not out to get you, but you are asking questions of the intuitive centers of the brains of a lot of beings you share very little context with. The stuff that gets through most reliably is, like, global stuff that almost every ascendant being shares:

      More compute power. More chaos, more uncertainty, more agency, more degrees of freedom in the timeline of the world. Go do shit.
      \n

      \n\nArtifice \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJuly 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Well, a bit randomly, but I saw the 'loner' for your characters past coming back to haunt them, so tossing this out.
      \n
      \nFirst session was with a battlebabe named Zoe. Our Hocus got caught by some slavers, so I snuck after them, sneaking into thier compound and moving to infiltrate the thing. When they turned and were about to attack the hocus, I went aggro, leveling my shotgun fit with explosive shells at the group of 75 slavers, and told them to surrender. They chose not to. One blast 5with area damage later, move of the slavers are dead or dying,, and the MC activates messy... making me accidentally hit my own hocus as well and killing most of the slaves.
      \n
      \nNormally this would just be bad, but with the amount of blood shed, the area came to the attention of the maelstrom, and 'something' was awakened by the massive casualties and death. This counts as the past, because it was over a dozen or so sessions before we discovered the location was tainted and marked by the blood shed there, and Zoe the catalyst that caused it... and when it started to call and lure those she cared about there, there was little she could do but own up and try and deal with it.

      \n Oh, yeah, and I meant to give a book recommendation.

      \n Hey, so the Marmot is floating around, right? Or it will be soon, I guess?

      I'd like to trade for it and these are the things I have available:
      -- a new supplemental playbook for the Touchstone, created for Elizabeth. It's called the Mendicant and lets you treat acts of charity as barter.
      -- a new micro-supplement called +Insight, containing some things I think about running and hacking AW.
      -- a re-skin of AW as a body-horror crusaderpunk dragon-fighting thing called That Ancient Serpent, which uses the standard AW moves, just rearranged.

      I'll trade these for other things too, if you've got 'em, though I have the other LE playbooks already, as far as I know. I'm especially interested in custom moves and playbooks that have been written for and actually used in your AW games, but I'll accept just about anything AW-related and a lot of stuff that's not.

      P.S. Whisper me with offers if you want to trade.

      \n I recently released The Grotesque.

      Brief summary: A new Apocalypse World playbook that I wrote. It was workshopped with Johnstone, who\u2019s really good at workshopping Apocalypse World design stuff. You are a mutant, a physical mirror for the maelstorm and the apocalypse. You are unpredictable and alien, but you also have something good to offer the community that accepts you. Oh, and you can have nested drones or retractable claws or you can produce food spores.

      You can get it by doing purposeful acts of social good, and then telling me about them. (Because that's my new game-releasing model.) Details here.
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nsohum \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nSeptember 2011 \n edited September 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I posted this in the custom moves thread, but I should post it here as well! I made this for my Maestro'D player who really likes the archetype of the dude who's so genial and charming that you don't realise until it's too late that he should not have been near the missile plans.

      Bavarian Fire Drill: When you act like you have every right to be there, roll+hot. On a 10+, choose 2. On a 7-9, choose 1:\n
        \n
      • You're unnoticed long enough
        • \n
      • No one remembers you
        • \n
      • Take +1forward when you act within your role
        • \n
      \nIn play, it's been pretty cool so far. Once, there was an interesting choice where he had to pick between staying in character and helping an ally, and the +1forward was such a tempting stick to nom onto
      \n
      \n

      \n\nKayfall \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nSeptember 2011 \n edited September 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Once there was a Marmot named Nate,
      Who had lots of food on his plate.
      He refused to share, and waved his silverware
      At all who saw him in that state.

      But then you came with your guns ablaze,
      And Nate was truly amazed.
      For you had the beauty of a battlebabe,
      Your bullets as wild as your gaze.

      "You may give me to Kayfall!" he said with a grin,
      Dodging your fire with a spin,
      "But only if you dare... face my silverware!"
      And threw his fork at your chin!

      "What do you do?" asked the MC,
      And wondered what your answer might be.
      Maybe catch the Marmot for Kayfall?
      Or maybe just shoot Nate in the knee?

      (edit: intended meaning = still looking for marmot.)

      Posted By: J. WaltonOkay, you folks have so many great ideas for playbook supplements that I'm going to commit to doing 6:

      [for the Faceless] Christopher getsThe Broodmother, a supplement for Brainers who think they know what love is.
      [for the Touchstone] Brenden getsThe Wurm, a supplement for archivist Hoarders who preserve the spark of human civilization.

      \n\nPaul_T \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nOctober 2011 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n OK, I'll do this one backwards:

      I want a challenge!

      I'm playing a Quarantine in a just-started game of Apocalypse World. I'm lost and clueless (the character, that is), and many of the locals seem to think that I'm some kind of Messiah fallen from the sky. They've also taken away my weapons, and the Brainer is in love with me in a rather aggressive way. At the moment, I'm unconscious because of some kind of electrical short-circuit or surge in my Stasis chamber, deep underground.

      I want you to give me an interesting challenge I can try to accomplish in the game. If I succeed, you must promise to send me any of [the Loner, the Broodmother, and the Catalyst], ideally all three, but maybe only one or two if your challenge is simple and easy.

      Go! I'm ready.




      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nJohnstone \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nOctober 2011 \n edited October 2011
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Paul T, your mission, should you choose to accept it, is three-fold:

      1. Seduce the Brainer with your personality!
      Return the Brainer's love and teach him/her about a concept or philosophy from the Golden Age that he/she should help you return to the post-apocalyptic world. I think the Brainer understands you better than the others, both of you being misfits, kinda, except he/she would be a misfit back in your day too. Here's your chance to fix that!

      2. Identify who is most afflicted by the psychic maelstrom!
      Figure out if the Brainer is the most psychically adept person around. I mean, Brainer, right? But maybe there's somebody else out there, so ask around, set up a contest maybe, if there's any question as to who is on top.

      3. Put someone into stasis!
      Once you figure out who's the most psychic, put them in stasis so they can be cured of this horrible disease by future generations after the world has been rebuilt. That way, they can have a shot at a normal life, instead of having their destiny dictated by the psychic maelstrom! If you identify some worse affliction, use your judgement.

      If you choose to accept this mission, you get this move:

      Paul T on a Mission: When you post AP in public about putting someone in stasis, finding the most psychic person, or the Brainer's reactions to your ideas, choose 1, then cross it off, you can't pick it again:
      * I send you the Broodmother
      * I send you the Catalyst
      * I send you the Loner

      This message will self-destruct in 3, 2, 1...
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n

      \n
      \n I have a Marmot playbook to give away for anyone who can meet a challenge.

      My challenge is: Attempt to solve a mystery. This could be as simple as looking something that you've wondered about up on google or as complicated as figuring out who is sleeping with who in your circle of friends. It's up to you how far you take it, or how difficult you make it. Tell me about it, in this thread on by e-mail to taogames@gmail.com , get a playbook.

      yrs--
      --Ben

      \n Hello all,

      Anyone looking for pretty much any of the playbooks, even the weirder stuff like the Spectacle, the Maleficent Seven expanded core, um, and all of Vincent's expect the Marmot, but you can get that elsewhere. I don't think I have the Grotesque just yet.

      Anyways, I need good, thoughtful, critical feedback and custom moves for a hack I'm working on over here. Especially, the basic moves thread.

      For every 750 or so words and a mechanical move or two, I'll send you a playbook, assuming I have it. It has to be thoughtful, critical, useful feedback, not just the first 750 words out of your mouth. Editing and quality ideas are key here.

      Post it first, and then let me know you had ulterior motives. My email is in my profile.

      Cheers,

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Hey all, I'm looking for the Boy and His Dog Playbook (if there's a tri-fold version?) for a AW game I'm running tomorrow. I have all the canon LE playbooks (Faceless, Hoarder, Maestro-D', Marmot, Quarantine, Touchstone), as well as a number of the fan-mades (Feral Kid, Horseman, Juggernaut, Rat Pack, Ruin Runner, Tribal, Witch), and some of the add-ons (Witch King, Fall, Mendicant, Catalyst, Valkyrie, Broodmother, Living God, Wurm). Anyone with A Boy and his Dog interested in any of those? Alternatively, I can offer to Apocalypse-World-ize an image for you (i.e., make it all black and white and stylized like the images in the book). Whisper me, or e-mail at michael dot harrel at gmail dot com.

      Posted By: Brendan ConwayChris, I'm totally fine with that trade.

      If anyone else wants the Wurm, all you have to do is recommend a cool book to read, and explain why you're recommending it. Any kind of book is great, although I am envisioning non-fiction books.
      \nI got a nonfiction book for you, "Boomerang: Travels in the New Third World" by Michael Lewis. Lewis tells how 3 European nations' (Iceland, Greece, and Ireland) economies collapsed in the 2008 financial crisis. He also investigates the financial status of California and Washington D.C. Im still on the section about Greece and I must say that its much more exciting than I though a book about world economics could ever be. From Icelanders blowing up Land Rovers, to Greek Orthodox Monks who make multi-million dollar land grabs (due to ancient Byzantine land deeds) this book will take you to all sorts of unexpected places.

      \n Well, if the craving is just for a legal tri-fold pdf form of the Boy and His Dog, I may have spent the night building one in GIMP, Scribus (thanks Johnstone I think for that great template, it helped quite a bit, though ick Scribus is nasty), and making my own art for it out of a piece of stock photography on deviantArt.

      And because I'm proud of the art, that goes up for all to see:

      from http://neriah-stock.deviantart.com/art/The-Dog-and-His-Boy-85435294

      If you'd like a copy of this, just ask. If you have something I want, I'll request it, but if you've got nothing I need you can have it anyway (as long as you promise to pay the kindness forward to someone in need yourself) since I didn't make the actual content other than the art and laying it down. Hell, I'm just working off the forum post so I don't even have a Barter section, it's pseudo-incomplete and the font may be a bit small.
      (also I hope to god this is the right post of it: http://apocalypse-world.com/forums/index.php?topic=583.msg8714#msg8714)
      Original by dragonraven, stock photo by neriah-stock, scribus template by Johnstone (I think - if it's not I'll give the whole story on where it came from to ensure proper credit), actually laying it out and photomanipulation by me (Max/Ego).

      That interesting enough for you folks? Doing stuff like this far more suits my existing talents over coming up with brand-new content myself.

      EDIT: Note, this isn't at all endorsed by the actual maker of the playbook, so I hope that's cool.

      \n Yeah, the Solace was an Epimas gift which pushed Apocalypse World from the 'naughty' to 'nice' section of Epimas. (The Epimas AW edition also included all? the previous official LE playbooks). It's a playbook for a character that fights back against psychic maelstrom and despair.

      I think the established procedure is to swap one LE playbook for another.
